In re Anonymous


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Kings County


106 Misc. 2d 792; 435 N.Y.S.2d 527; 1981 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2019



January 22, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was the petition by an unmarried 22-year-old male that he be allowed to adopt an unmarried 26-year-old male with whom he shared a home and a homosexual relationship.


OVERVIEW: The parties, a homosexual couple, wished to enter into an adoptive relationship to establish a legally cognizable relationship in order to facilitate inheritance, the handling of their insurance policies and pension plans, and the acquisition of suitable housing. The court determined that the parties were aware of the alternatives available to them to achieve this goal, that they were not attempting to use the adult adoption statute to create, in effect, a pseudo-marriage, and that they were not in violation of any criminal statute. The court found that New York provided for the adoption of adults, and that the best interests standard was applicable to any adoption. The best interests standard may not be used to thwart an adult adoption between two competent consenting adults which is sought for valid legal and economic reasons. The court found no public policy or public morality considerations which operated as a bar to an adoption between two consenting adult males who were engaged in a homosexual relationship. The court granted the adoption.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition of adoption by an unmarried 22-year-old male of an unmarried 26-year-old male with whom he shared a home and a homosexual relationship.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Adoption -- Adoption of Adult -- Homosexual Relationship

Since the Legislature has taken statutory notice of the significant difference between adult and minor adoptions by virtue of not requiring parental consent in adult adoptions (Domestic Relations Law, § 111, subd 4) and since the Legislature, by its deliberately broad definition of an adoption proceeding (Domestic Relations Law, § 110), has taken notice of the many legal and economic purposes which may motivate an adult adoption, the "best interests of the child" standard applicable to any adoption may not be used to thwart an adult adoption, sought for valid legal and economic reasons, between an unmarried 22-year-old male and a 26-year-old male who have a homosexual relationship; there are no public policy or public morality considerations which operate as a bar to the adoption since a consensual homosexual relationship between adults is no longer a crime in New York (see People v Onofre, 51 NY2d 476) and judicial interference with the statutory right of adult adoption, because of the sexual preference of the parties, out of view of the public and not connected with their reasons for an adoptive relationship,  [***2] would not advance the cause of public morality.

 

1964 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Shirpsen Realty Corp. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Kings County


107 Misc. 2d 714; 435 N.Y.S.2d 896; 1981 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2088



January 21, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff realty corporation filed an action against defendant, the city, finance commissioner, and attorney general, seeking to have N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 22 and New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § C-17 declared unconstitutional and to invalidate a tax lien assessed by the city. The city filed an action against the realty corporation seeking reimbursement for money paid for the demolition of a building. The court addressed the actions jointly.


OVERVIEW: The realty corporation owned an apartment and owed delinquent taxes. Fire occurred on the premises and the corporation settled with its insurance company. The city began unsafe building procedures. Demolition was ordered, and the city demanded reimbursement, pursuant to New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § C-17 et seq., against the fire insurance proceeds. Both parties initiated actions, the corporation against the city, its finance commissioner, and attorney general, asserting that the city could not demolish the premises and then assert a lien pursuant to N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 22 and New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § C-17 et seq., and that the statutes exceeded constitutional authority. The city's action sought demolition costs. The court ruled in favor of the city. The court found that the corporation did not meet its burden of establishing the invalidity of the statutes, as the interest in taking the profit out of arson by allowing the city to collect its taxes was valid on its face. Further, because the corporation did nothing to demonstrate any intention to restore the premises, the statutes were valid as applied to it, as well, and the court awarded the city demolition costs.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the realty corporation's action.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal Corporations -- Claims against Fire Insurance Proceeds -- Demolition Costs

 Section 22 of the General Municipal Law and title C of chapter 17 of the Administrative Code of the City of New York (§ C17-1 et seq.), which create a lien against fire insurance proceeds for real property tax arrears in order to take the profit out of arson by allowing the municipality to collect its taxes out of the fire insurance proceeds unless the funds are used to restore the property, are constitutional on their face, plaintiff, whose building was demolished by defendant City of New York pursuant to court order more than one year after a fire, having failed to meet its burden of establishing the invalidity of the statutes beyond a reasonable doubt; the statutes are not invalid as applied to plaintiff since plaintiff ignored all prior notices and did nothing to demonstrate any intention to restore the premises; in addition, the city is entitled to offset its actual demolition costs against the fire insurance proceeds inasmuch as plaintiff was the record owner responsible for the costs of the demolition.

In re Estate of Brown


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Surrogate's Court of New York, New York County


107 Misc. 2d 970; 436 N.Y.S.2d 132; 1981 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2119



January 14, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney sought original probate (New York) of decedent's last will and testament and requested to be appointed executor and trustee pursuant to N.Y. Surr. Ct. Proc. Act § 1605. Decedent died a domiciliary of Florida but she was buried in New York and had approximately half of her assets in New York. The will was drafted and executed in New York while she was a domiciliary, prior to her move to Florida.


OVERVIEW: The attorney could not be appointed in Florida as the personal representative of the decedent's estate because Fla. Stat. Ann. § 733.304 prohibited a nonresident from qualifying as a personal representative, executor, or administrator unless that person was related to the decedent. The attorney did not qualify under § 733.304 and so he could not qualify in Florida under its statutes. The court found that whether or not the Florida statute was constitutional, an issue that was up for debate, original probate could be granted under N.Y. Surr. Ct. Proc. Act § 1605. Section 1605(2)(c) permitted original probate where the laws of a testator's domicile discriminated against domiciliaries of New York either as a beneficiary or a fiduciary. The court concluded that because the Florida law discriminated against nonresidents such as the attorney, the proceeding came within the purview of § 1605. Additionally, the court noted that no probate proceeding had been commenced in Florida. Consequently, the will could be originally probated in New York even if Florida did not discriminate, pursuant to § 1605(1).


OUTCOME: The court entertained jurisdiction to probate the will.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Executors and Administrators -- Estate of Nondomiciliary -- Original Probate

A New York Surrogate's Court has jurisdiction to probate the will of decedent, who died a domiciliary of Florida but is buried in New York and left approximately 50% of her assets in New York, her former domicile, since the proposed executor of the estate, a New York attorney who is not related to decedent, is prohibited from serving as decedent's representative by Florida statute; original probate can be granted in New York pursuant to SCPA 1605 (subd 2, par [c]), which permits original probate where the laws of testator's domicile discriminate against domiciliaries of New York either as beneficiaries or fiduciaries, or pursuant to subdivision 1 of said statute, since no probate proceeding has been commenced in Florida.

 

1966 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rosenbaum


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Rockland County


107 Misc. 2d 501; 435 N.Y.S.2d 502; 1981 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2060



January 9, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following indictment on numerous counts of larceny, defendant nursing home operator filed motions for inspection of the grand jury minutes and dismissal of the indictment as being vague and lacking in sufficient specificity so as to identify the charges brought against, or alternatively, for enumerated items of discovery and a bill of particulars.


OVERVIEW: The operator was indicted on numerous counts of larceny based on charges that he, inter alia, commingled personal allowance funds, and committed thefts of certain Supplemental Security Income checks and Social Security checks from former residents. The operator filed a motion to inspect the grand jury minutes and a motion to dismiss the indictment, or alternatively, for certain specified items of discovery and a bill of particulars. The court denied the motions. The court held that the operator had no good faith claim of right to retain and possess the checks in question, and the operator did not have lawful possession of them. The proof at the grand jury appeared legally sufficient to support each and every count charged, and the operator's motion to dismiss for lack of evidence was denied on that ground. The court also found that the prosecutor did not fail to provide the grand jury with proper legal instructions, and the operator failed to demonstrate that the prosecutor knowingly withheld any evidence which could lend support to the operator's claim of right argument.


OUTCOME: The operator's motion to dismiss for vagueness, lack of specificity, and lack of evidence was denied. The prosecutor consented to provide the operator with a full bill of particulars as to the count charging the operator with commingling of personal allowance funds.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- Larceny -- Claim of Right Defense

It is a sufficient defense to a larceny charge that the property was appropriated openly and avowedly under a claim of title proffered in good faith, even though such claim is untenable; however, the theory of claim of right, now contained in subdivision 1 of section 155.15 of the Penal Law, does not excuse the retention of the property of another to offset or pay demand held against him. Accordingly, the contention of defendant, the operator of a home for adults who was charged with the theft of certain Supplemental Security Income (SSI) and Social Security checks from former residents of the home, that he is entitled to the checks in question under a claim of right arising from his "substantial reliance" upon information contained in a civil audit showing outstanding moneys allegedly owing to him by New York State and, alternatively, that under an unsubstantiated "30-day rule" the owner of an adult home may keep open a bed upon discharge of a resident for 30 days beyond the actual discharge date, which rule affords him a lawful claim to take those SSI and Social Security checks which were issued for the month covered by this alleged [***2] "grace period", is without merit; clearly, lacking any basis in law giving him a good faith claim of right to retain and possess the checks in question, defendant here did not have lawful possession of them and, in the absence of such a claim of right, any claimed "offset" is irrelevant.

 

1967 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re G.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, Schenectady County


107 Misc. 2d 900; 436 N.Y.S.2d 546; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2914



December 30, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner department of social services (DSS) filed an action to commit the guardianship and custody of a minor child to the DSS under N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 384-b and to terminate respondent natural father's right to refuse to consent to the child's adoption. Petitioner foster parents filed an action seeking the direct adoption of the child, setting forth alternative grounds for dispensing with parental consent under N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 111.


OVERVIEW: After being voluntarily placed in foster care, the child was placed in the custody of the foster parents, who continuously cared for the child since he was three months old. At the time the related petitions were filed by the DSS and the foster parents, the natural father was incarcerated in another state for an aggravated robbery conviction. The court granted the DSS's petition and subsequently granted the foster parents' petition for direct adoption. The court held that N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 111(2)(d) dispensed with the natural father's parental consent to the adoption because the natural father had been deprived of his civil rights by virtue of his assault conviction. The court further held that the application of § 111(2)(d) did not violate substantive due process or equal protection because the state had a compelling interest in achieving permanency in the parent-child relationship for children whose natural parents were unable or unwilling to provide continuous, stable, and long-term care and because the adoption without the natural father's consent was substantially related to the legitimate state interest in achieving such permanency.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition filed by the DSS to commit the guardianship and custody of a minor child to the DSS and subsequently granted the foster parents' petition for direct adoption of the child.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Adoption -- Consent -- Dispensing with Parental Consent because of Incarceration

1. An out-of-State felony conviction and sentence results in a loss of civil rights (Civil Rights Law, § 79) for purposes of a statute which dispenses with parental consent to an adoption for a parent "who has been deprived of civil rights pursuant to the civil rights law and whose civil rights have not been restored" (Domestic Relations Law, § 111, subd 2, par [d]) since dispensing with parental consent in an adoption proceeding on the basis of a non-New York State conviction which would be a felony in New York furthers the legitimate State objective of achieving permanency for children by removing legal barriers to their adoption; in addition, the statute eliminating the need for parental consent because of incarceration is not unconstitutionally overbroad on its face since termination of parental consent requirements for adoption because of a criminal conviction and sentence has no "chilling effect" on the exercise of parental rights and, in any event, constitutional issues concerning parental rights must be determined on the basis of the application of the statute to the actual facts of [***2] each case rather than on the basis of facial validity.

Adoption -- Consent -- Dispensing with Parental Consent because of Incarceration

2. When there has been a separation of parent from child at early infancy, followed by an extended prison sentence of the father and an integration of the child into the family unit of foster parents, the State can validly terminate the father's parental rights and grant an adoption to the foster parents based solely on the child's best interests without a specific finding of unfitness; accordingly, in light of respondent's 1979 Texas robbery conviction and 5- to 15-year prison sentence, the absence of any functional relationship between respondent and his child, the substantial future period before respondent could begin to create such relationship and the close familial ties between the child and the foster-adoptive parents, dispensing with respondent's consent to the adoption because of his incarceration (Domestic Relations Law, § 111, subd 2, par [d]) does not violate due process or equal protection inasmuch as granting the adoption is in the child's best interests and bears a substantial relation to the legitimate State interest [***3] of achieving permanency for children whose parents are unable or unwilling to provide stable long-term continuous care and superimposing a constitutional requirement of a preliminary finding of parental unfitness would not accomplish any greater protection of respondent's rights without sacrificing or unduly postponing achievement of the goal of permanency.

 

1968 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Forrest v. Ambach


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


107 Misc. 2d 920; 436 N.Y.S.2d 119; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2915



December 11, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was a proceeding, filed pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, that sought to invalidate a decision of respondent education commissioner, which dismissed the appeal of petitioner school psychologist's petition for her reinstatement.


OVERVIEW: The education commissioner had issued a decision that dismissed the petition of the school psychologist that sought her reinstatement. In response, she filed a proceeding pursuant to article 78 that sought to invalidate the commissioner's decision. The court issued a judgment in her favor, and remanded for further administrative proceedings to develop fully the record concerning her petition for reinstatement as a school psychologist. The court agreed with the commissioner's findings that the record in this case provided insufficient basis for concluding that she was eligible for tenure or that she gained tenure by acquiescence when her services were continued beyond the probationary period. However, the school board could not terminate her services for a constitutionally impermissible purpose. Further, her pleadings that she was injured by the school board's alleged misconduct that resulted in the loss of her job was sufficient for her to be an aggrieved party within the meaning of N.Y. Educ. Law § 310.


OUTCOME: The court issued a judgment in the school psychologist's favor, and remanded for further administrative proceedings to develop fully the record concerning her petition for reinstatement as a school psychologist.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Schools -- School Psychologist -- Tenure

1. A school psychologist employed part time on a four-day per week basis is not eligible for tenure and did not gain tenure by acquiescence when her services were continued beyond the usual probationary period, since service as a part-time employee does not constitute probationary service and does not lead to eligibility for tenure.

Schools -- School Psychologist -- Dismissal Due to Alleged Compliance with Regulations

2. Although petitioner, an untenured part-time school psychologist, served at the will of the school board, she could not be terminated for a constitutionally impermissible purpose; petitioner has standing in a CPLR article 78 proceeding in which she alleged that she had been dismissed solely because she adhered to professional obligations to perform evaluations of handicapped children in the manner required under newly enacted State and Federal laws and regulations, since she has affirmatively alleged that she was injured by the board's alleged misconduct in that it resulted in the loss of her job, and the Commissioner of Education's determination not to decide whether the school board was neglecting its statutory [***2] duty regarding handicapped children resulted in a failure of petitioner to have her grievance aired and as such was arbitrary and capricious. If petitioner was in fact dismissed solely due to her attempt to adhere to statutory mandates and her own professional standards as a psychologist, her dismissal would be arbitrary, capricious and unconstitutional, and accordingly, the matter is remanded to the Commissioner of Education to resolve the issues of alleged neglect of statutory duties regarding handicapped children in the district and whether said neglect resulted in the termination of petitioner's services for a constitutionally impermissible purpose.

 

1969 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Silverman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, New York County


106 Misc. 2d 468; 434 N.Y.S.2d 319; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2774



December 8, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, defendant's motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to dismiss his indictment on charges of larceny on the ground that the evidence before the grand jury which constituted commercial bribe receiving was insufficient to also constitute larceny.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with multiple counts of commercial bribe receiving and one court of larceny. Defendant was an employee of a textile manufacturer and was responsible for setting prices for goods sold. Defendant sold goods below the retail value to third parties that in turn re-sold the goods sharing a portion of the profits with defendant personally. Defendant moved to dismiss the larceny charges contending that conduct, which constituted commercial bribe receiving, could not also constitute larceny. The court denied the motion, saying that the same conduct may constitute more than one crime and that they may all be charged in the same indictment. The court defined the elements of larceny by embezzlement, which required a conversion of property belonging to another, which had been entrusted to the embezzler. Although defendant was authorized to sell the goods, he was not authorized to sell the goods below their market value and receive kickbacks for his own account. Selling the goods on the terms he did was an unauthorized assumption of rights of ownership over goods belonging to another, which constituted conversion.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the larceny indictment against him because the action of selling his employer's property below its market value in exchange for kickbacks from the purchasers constituted a conversion of the property and larceny by embezzlement.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Commercial Bribe Receiving -- Larceny

Conduct which constitutes commercial bribe receiving may also constitute larceny (Penal Law, § 155.05) and, therefore, defendant, who, as merchandise manager of a textile fabric manufacturer, sold his employer's goods, at a price below market value, to jobbers and then shared in the profits achieved through the resale of the fabrics at higher prices, may lawfully be prosecuted for both crimes inasmuch as he wrongfully obtained a portion of the value of his employer's fabrics; defendant's conduct also constitutes larceny by embezzlement since he "converted" to his own use goods which were entrusted to him to sell for the benefit of his employer, the property embezzled being the difference between the full market value of the goods sold by defendant to the jobbers and the value actually received by the employer and/or the fabrics which were to have been sold by defendant on behalf of his employer but which he in effect sold on his own account; a finding that defendant's conduct constitutes larceny as well as commercial bribe receiving does not render the larceny statute unconstitutionally [***2] vague.

 

1970 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Long Beach Housing Authority v. Lew Chew Soon Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Nassau County


107 Misc. 2d 1037; 436 N.Y.S.2d 539; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2921



December 8, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In condemnation proceedings, respondent claimant filed a motion to compel petitioner condemnor to make an offer and an advance payment pursuant to N.Y. Em. Dom. Proc. Law §§ 303, 304.


OVERVIEW: The original owner of the property defaulted on a mortgage. The United States government took an assignment after paying off the bank. Four days after such assignment, a county tax lien arose. The county tax lien was sold to the claimant. Before delivery of the tax deed, however, the United State's foreclosed on the property. The condemnor received a deed through the foreclosure sale. No notice of the foreclosure was given to the claimant, although the United State's was aware of the tax sale. In denying claimant's motion to compel the condemnor to make an offer of payment, the court held that the condemnor's title was superior. In so ruling, the court stated that the United State's lien, which arose upon assignment, was first in time to the county's tax lien. As such, the condemnor, whose title derived from the United States, prevailed. The court rejected the claimant's contention that his lien was superior because the condemnor did not exercise its right of redemption under N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 1020(1). In so ruling, the court held that, under the Supremacy Clause of the United State's Constitution, the state was not permitted to impair the United State's lien.


OUTCOME: The court denied the claimant's motion to compel the condemnor to make an offer and an advance payment in condemnation proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Mortgages -- Federally Insured Mortgage -- Priority over Tax Deed

Since the guarantee of the mortgage indebtedness on the subject property by the Federal Housing Authority and the subsequent assignment to the Federal Government of the defaulted Federally insured mortgage occurred before the lien for unpaid local real estate taxes became fixed, the first in time, first in right rule governs the priority of liens and petitioner, whose title derives from the Federal Government through a mortgage foreclosure sale, must prevail over claimant whose title is based on a tax deed; local laws cannot extinguish the rights of the Federal Government in property and since the Government lien is paramount, the simple failure to give notice to the tax lien purchaser cannot cloak that person with any greater rights than he originally possessed and any attempt to do so on procedural grounds must fail as an unconstitutional attempt to divest the Government of its superior rights; the mortgage cannot be deemed discharged because of the mortgagee's failure to exercise its right of redemption (Real Property Tax Law, § 1024) since the statute may not be construed to affect [***2] the lien interest of Federally owned mortgages which were acquired prior to the attachment of a lien for unpaid taxes.

 

1971 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Grinspan v. Adirondack Park Agency


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Warren County


106 Misc. 2d 501; 434 N.Y.S.2d 90; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2781



November 15, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding to annul a determination of respondent Adirondack Park Agency (New York), which disapproved the property owner's application for approval of a three-lot subdivision and a shoreline variance, and for an order directing the Agency to approve the plan as submitted by the landowner and to grant the variance requested. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The property owner sought subdivision approval and a shoreline setback variance for a six-acre lot he owned on the Hudson River. When permission was denied, he brought an action against the Agency. He alleged that there was an unconstitutional delegation of police power when the legislature delegated to the Agency the authority to promulgate setback requirements. The court held that because N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law § 15-2701 et seq. contained sufficiently clear standards and guidelines within which the Agency could properly exercise its discretion, the delegation was proper. The setback restrictions were not unconstitutional, illegal, or invalid although they were not promulgated for the purposes of public health, safety, and morals; aesthetic principles were an acceptable basis for land use restrictions. The regulation was entitled to a strong presumption of constitutionality, and the property owner did not meet his burden of establishing that the setback restriction was irrational and unconstitutional. The Agency's action did not effect an unconstitutional taking of private property; the owner was not deprived of the reasonable use or of a reasonable return on his property.


OUTCOME: The court denied the property owner's motion for summary judgment and granted the Agency's summary judgment motion. The Agency's request to transfer the art. 78 proceeding to the appellate division was denied.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Environmental Conservation -- Wild, Scenic and Recreational Rivers System Act -- Structural Setback Restrictions

The 150-foot structural setback restriction for all structures located in a recreational river area promulgated by the Adirondack Park Agency pursuant to its statutory authority under the Rivers System Act to "make and enforce regulations necessary for the management, protection, and enhancement of and control of land use and development in the wild, scenic and recreational river areas" ( ECL 15-2709, subd 1) does not constitute an unconstitutional delegation of the police power since the provisions of the Rivers System Act contain sufficiently clear standards and guidelines within which the agency can properly exercise its discretion; since preservation of the aesthetic quality of a project site constitutes a valid exercise of the police power, the agency's determination that the structural setback should be 150 feet in order to ensure that the natural scenic and recreational qualities of the designated river are protected from improvident development is not arbitrary or capricious; even if the setback restriction will cause a diminution in the market value of petitioner's [***2] property along the Hudson River, such diminution does not in and of itself constitute an unlawful and unconstitutional taking of property without compensation and there is no showing that petitioner has been deprived of the reasonable use of or a reasonable return on his property.

 

1972 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Sea Lar Trading Co. v. Michael


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


107 Misc. 2d 93; 433 N.Y.S.2d 403; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2833



November 14, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner cigarette wholesaler commenced suit against respondent Commissioner of the Department of Finance of New York City (finance commissioner) and sought judgment declaring New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code §§ D46-15.0 and D46-17.0 unconstitutional, annulling certain warrants, restraining notices of sale, and annulling a notice of postseizure hearing.


OVERVIEW: The finance commissioner seized 2,300 cartons of cigarettes, three tax meters, and all the tax stamps in possession of a cigarette wholesaler on the basis that the cigarette wholesaler forged the tax meter imprints on the cartons. The cigarette wholesaler commenced suit, and sought judgment declaring New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code §§ D46-15.0 and D46-17.0 unconstitutional, annulling certain warrants, restraining notice and notices of sale, and annulling a notice of postseizure hearing. The court granted the motion and held that the cigarette wholesaler was entitled to a hearing. The court held: (1) the seizure, and proposed sale of the unstamped cigarettes was an invalid act by the finance commissioner because the cigarette wholesaler was entitled to a hearing before the cigarettes were sold; (2) the seizure of the items prior to a hearing was not required, however, the imposition of the payment of the tax prior to a hearing was tantamount to the preclusion of the right to due process; and (3) the statutory scheme was not required to be invalidated because the court had the power to disregard provisions of the statute that was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted the cigarette wholesaler's petition and issued a judgment that portions of a state statute were unconstitutional, but refused to strike the whole statutory scheme, and held that the cigarette wholesaler was entitled to a hearing on the merits of the seizure.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Taxation -- Cigarette Tax -- Revocation of Tax Agency and Seizure of Unstamped Cigarettes

1. Since the appointment of petitioner, a licensed cigarette wholesaler, as an agent to affix tax stamps to cigarette packages does not amount to a franchise or license, both of which cannot be suspended or revoked without a hearing, petitioner's status is no more than an agent whose agency is terminable at will and, therefore, the suspension of petitioner's agency by respondent New York City Department of Finance without a hearing because of alleged forgeries is valid; however, the seizure, and proposed sale of unstamped cigarettes in petitioner's possession (Administrative Code of City of New York, § D46-17.0) is invalid as a violation of due process even though petitioner has been offered a postseizure hearing since there is no statute nor any departmental rule requiring a postseizure hearing except at the whim of respondent; the seizure of the tax meters used by petitioner is likewise invalid since no arrest has been made nor any judicial warrant issued and the fact that the meters may have been evidence of the alleged crime of forgery does not give respondent any right to seize them.

 [***2] Taxation -- Cigarette Tax -- Seizure of Tax Agent's Assets to Satisfy Tax Deficiency

2. Respondent New York City Department of Finance, based upon a determination that petitioner, a licensed cigarette wholesaler and appointed tax agent to affix tax stamps to cigarette packages, owed taxes, acted lawfully in issuing an immediate tax warrant, filing it as a judgment and then seizing all of petitioner's assets by way of a levy prior to a hearing; however, since due process requires that a prompt postseizure hearing subject to judicial review be made available and that access to judicial review not be unduly burdened, the statutory provision requiring the full payment of the tax as a precondition to the allowance of judicial review of the propriety of the determination after hearing (Administrative Code of City of New York, § D46-11.0), effectively deprives petitioner of the opportunity to obtain any judicial review and is thereby violative of due process; granting petitioner access to the courts for a review of the tax determination without the imposition of the improper burden satisfies the demands of due process without having to invalidate the entire statutory scheme.

 

1973 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Van Hoesen v. Hogan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


107 Misc. 2d 264; 433 N.Y.S.2d 709; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2857



November 12, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion and cross motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff insured's breach of contract complaint for fire loss coverage as time barred by the policy's terms. Defendant adjuster filed a cross-motion to dismiss the insured's claim for negligent appraisal of losses, and all cross-claims as untimely, and for failure to state a claim.


OVERVIEW: The insured sustained fire losses at his premises. She sought to recover on his insurance policy, which contained a standard provision that prohibited an action unless it was commenced within two years of the loss's inception. The insurer filed a motion to dismiss on the ground that the claim was time-barred under the contract. The adjuster sought dismissal for failure to state a claim, and for untimeliness. The court granted the insurer's motion and the adjuster's cross-motion to dismiss, concluding that N.Y. C.P.L.R. 214(4) was inapplicable to the insurance policy because that limitation period applied to actions for property damage, not one for breach of an insurance contract. Thus, the two-year limitation period of the policy governed the insured's action because it did not violate public policy or constitutional law. Allegations of estoppel were rejected for lack of evidence, and for failure to raise the issue in the complaint. Finally, the negligent appraisal claim against the adjuster failed because it was untimely, and the adjuster owed no duty to the insured.


OUTCOME: The court granted the insurer's motion to dismiss, and the adjuster's cross-motion to dismiss the insured's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Insurance -- Fire Insurance -- Two-Year Limitation for Commencing Action on Policy

An insured's action against an insurance company to recover for a fire loss under the terms of a fire insurance policy is governed by the policy's two-year limitation period which prohibits any action for the recovery of a claim upon the policy unless commenced within two years after inception of the loss (Insurance Law, § 168, subd 5); the shorter limitation period is not prohibited by public policy and is not constitutionally infirm; plaintiff insured's allegations that defendant insurer should be estopped from asserting the limitation period are insufficient to defeat defendant's dismissal motion since estoppel was not pleaded in the complaint and the affidavit of plaintiff's attorney containing conclusory allegations does not supply the requisite evidentiary showing; the agent of the insurer who allegedly negligently conducted an appraisal of plaintiff's loss has the benefit of the short limitation period specified in the insurance agreement and, thus, the action is dismissed as to him also.

 

1974 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lent


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Westchester County


105 Misc. 2d 831; 433 N.Y.S.2d 538; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2567



November 10, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, defendant's motion to suppress is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in a single-count indictment with the possession of a gravity knife. Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence that was seized incident to his arrest, which was based upon a warranted that unbeknownst to the arresting officers had been vacated.


OVERVIEW: A warrant was issued for defendant's arrest in connection with charges of kidnapping. Defendant surrendered, the charges were reduced, and he was released on his own recognizance. The arrest warrant was vacated. However, the fact that the warrant had been vacated was not communicated to the police precinct in the city where defendant lived. Subsequently, defendant was arrested on the basis of the warrant. Incident to his arrest defendant was searched, and a knife was found in his possession. He was charged with possession of a gravity knife. Defendant filed a motion to suppress. The court denied the motion. The court held that the police had sufficient probable cause to arrest defendant under the authority of the teletype communication of the warrant charging defendant with a serious crime, to search him contemporaneously thereunder, and to seize the knife. The mere fact that the police did not know that the warrant had been vacated earlier that day in another city did not alter their right and duty to arrest defendant when he was observed in their jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to suppress.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Unlawful Search and Seizure

Property seized incidental to a good faith arrest, based on an arrest warrant which unbeknownst to the officers had been vacated earlier in the day, need not be suppressed where there was sufficient probable cause for the arrest and the accompanying search and seizure.

 

1975 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. M & R Records, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Criminal Term, Suffolk County


106 Misc. 2d 1052; 432 N.Y.S.2d 846; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2811; 212 U.S.P.Q. (BNA) 797



November 6, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a motion to dismiss their indictments for manufacture of unauthorized recording of sound, advertisement and sale of unauthorized receding of sound, and failure to disclose origin of recording of sound, on the grounds that federal statutes preempted the state statutes under which they were indicted.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with manufacturing unauthorized recordings of sound in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 275.05, advertisement and sale of unauthorized recording of sale in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 275.10, and failure to disclose origin of recording of sound in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 275.15. Defendants moved to have the indictments dismissed on the grounds that the state statutes were, for chronological reasons, barred by federal statutes. The court rejected defendant's argument where 17 U.S.C.S. § 301 did not limit any rights or remedies under state statutes commenced before January 1, 1978. While the statutes in issue had been recodified, the court found that because the sections showed an intention to carry on and continue the statute upon which they were based, they did not create new rights and remedies not existing at the time of the enactment of 17 U.S.C.S. § 301.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to dismiss indictments was denied where the state statutes under which defendants were indicted were not preempted by a federal statute's chronological requirement where the new statutes were continuations of prior law.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- Manufacture and Sale of "Pirated" Sound Recordings -- Pre-emption by Federal Copyright Laws

A prosecution for the manufacture and sale of "pirated" sound recordings "fixed" (US Code, tit 17, § 101) on or before February 15, 1972, under State statutes effective September 1, 1978 (Penal Law, §§ 275.05, 275.10), is not pre-empted and therefore, barred by Federal copyright laws, which provide that any rights or remedies involving recordings "fixed" prior to February 15, 1972 are to be governed exclusively by Federal law except for any State remedies in effect prior to January 1, 1978 (US Code, tit 17, § 301) since the 1978 Penal Law enactments are merely extensions and re-enactments of previous General Business Law statutes relating to "pirated" recordings and did not create new rights and remedies not existing at the time of the enactment of the Federal copyright statute; the statute which prohibits offering a record for sale whose cover, box or jacket does not clearly disclose the manufacturer and name of the actual performer (Penal Law, § 275.15) is a consumer protect statute, not a copyright statute, and does not require that the recording be "fixed" and violations [***2] thereof are therefore not pre-empted by the Federal copyright laws which require that the sound recordings be "fixed" on or after February 15, 1972; a prosecution for the manufacture, advertisement and sale of unauthorized recordings of "live" performances (Penal Law, § 275.05, subd 2; § 275.10, subd 2) is not barred by the Federal act since there is no requirement that the recordings have been "fixed".

 

1976 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Howell v. Benson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


105 Misc. 2d 757; 432 N.Y.S.2d 835; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2582



October 31, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner cab driver filed a motion pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to compel respondent Commissioner of Public Safety of the City of Albany (New York) to make a determination on the cab driver's license applications.


OVERVIEW: The cab driver filed applications for four licenses. Almost 20 months elapsed since the first application was filed, but the Commissioner had not processed the applications. The cab driver filed a motion to compel a determination by the Commissioner. The court granted the motion. The court noted that the cab driver was not seeking a declaration requiring the issuance of the applications in his favor. He merely sought a judgment requiring the Commissioner to perform its mandated ministerial duty to make a determination. The duty did not involve the exercise of judgment or discretion. Accordingly, mandamus was available to the cab driver. The court ruled that it could not rule on the cab driver's motion that the Commissioner revoke the licenses of other cabs that were allegedly unconstitutional because the cab driver did not have status as an aggrieved party pending the determination on his applications.


OUTCOME: The court granted the cab driver's motion.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Proceeding against Body or Officer -- Pleadings -- Verified Answer

In a CPLR article 78 proceeding in the nature of mandamus brought to compel respondent Commissioner of Public Safety to make a determination on the petitioner's taxicab license applications submitted more than 12 months earlier, respondent's answer, which consisted of only a general denial without affidavits or written proof to explain its inaction, is insufficient as a matter of law to establish a triable issue of fact ( CPLR 7804, subd [d]) and consequently respondent is ordered to make a determination; however, petitioner may not have a judgment declaring certain other taxi companies improperly licensed since it cannot be determined whether petitioner has standing as an aggrieved party until respondent makes its determination as to petitioner's applications.

 

1977 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Regan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Onondaga County


107 Misc. 2d 37; 432 N.Y.S.2d 823; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2822



October 27, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district brought an action for declaratory judgment after defendant state comptroller reduced the district's state aid. The comptroller moved to dismiss the complaint and for summary judgment on the grounds that the complaint failed to state a cause of action. The school district cross-moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: N.Y. State Fin. Law § 99-c allowed school districts to receive health insurance reserve funds, but if the school district cancelled its health insurance with the State and defaulted in its obligation to repay the health insurance funds, its State assistance was to be reduced. 1977 N.Y. Laws 71, § 8(b) directed the commissioner of education to reduce a school district's budget by an amount of health insurance reserves unreimbursed if the school district filed a notice of intent to leave the State employee health plan. The school district in the instant case received health insurance reserve funds and later withdrew from the State health plan. The district's State aid was reduced by the amount of the health insurance reserves, and the comptroller also wanted to reduce a subsequent year's State aid. The court held that 1977 N.Y. Laws 71, § 8(b) prevailed over inconsistent provisions of N.Y. State Fin. Law § 99-c and that the school district had already repaid the health insurance reserve funds with the first deduction from its State aid.


OUTCOME: The court denied the comptroller's motion for summary judgment and granted the summary judgment motion of the school district.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Municipal Corporations -- School Districts -- Reduction in State Aid Apportionment

An August 7, 1977 agreement between plaintiff school district and the State Education Department whereby plaintiff agreed to repay the department for moneys advanced it from the Health Insurance Reserve Receipts Fund (HIRRF) in the event of its withdrawal from the State health insurance plan is unenforceable, since the statutory authority for the repayment called for by the agreement (State Finance Law, § 99-c, subds 1, 2) was repealed, by the subsequent enactment of an inconsistent statute (L 1977, ch 71, § 8, subd b), prior to the execution of said agreement, and, accordingly, plaintiff is under no obligation to reimburse HIRRF or the State for the sum received in 1977; application of both statutes would result in a school district that happened to be participating in the State health insurance plan as of March 25, 1977 and later withdrew from the plan being liable for up to twice the amount advanced, a result which school districts that were not participating in the program as of March 25, 1977 avoid.

 

1978 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


State v. Strong Oil Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


105 Misc. 2d 803; 433 N.Y.S.2d 345; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2565



October 23, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney general sought, pursuant to N.Y. Exec. Law § 63(12), to enforce N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 396-r against respondent corporation. In response, the corporation filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Section 396-r was an attempt by the state legislature to declare whether or not abnormal market conditions existed, and then to impose de facto price controls on home heating fuel, among other commodities, upon such a determination. After the state legislature declared an abnormal disruption for the 1979-1980 heating season, the attorney general brought the action against the corporation. The corporation denied the allegations of the petition and challenged the constitutionality of § 396-r. The corporation asserted § 396-r was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, was pre-empted by Federal statutes and thus in violation of the supremacy clause of the United States Constitution, and otherwise in violation of the due process clauses in the State and Federal Constitutions. On the corporation's motion to dismiss, the court held § 396-r was a price control statute and was therefore unconstitutional in that it conflicted with the Emergency Petroleum Allocation Act of 1973, 15 U.S.C.S. § 751 et seq. and its implementing directives and regulations which exempted home heating oil from price regulation, an area in which Congress intended to occupy the entire field.


OUTCOME: The court granted the corporation's motion to dismiss the attorney general's action.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Constitutional Law -- Supremacy Clause -- Federal Pre-emption of State Law

1. The two-pronged test for determining whether a State statute is preempted by Federal laws and thus invalid under the supremacy clause (US Const, art VI, § 2) is first, whether Congress has prohibited State regulation of the particular field involved, that is, whether Congress has chosen to completely "occupy the field to the exclusion of the States" in which case the States may not regulate within the field even where the regulation is in harmony with the Federal scheme, and, second, where Congress has chosen not to completely occupy a particular field, whether a State law is void to the extent that it conflicts with a valid Federal statute and "stands as an obstacle to the accomplishment and execution of the full purposes and objectives of Congress"; the intent of Congress to completely occupy a particular field and thereby preclude any State regulation thereof may be found from either an "explicit statement" in the Federal statute or implied from that statute's "structure and purpose" and deciding whether a State statute is in conflict with a Federal statute and hence invalid under the supremacy [***2] clause is a two-step process of first ascertaining the construction of the two statutes and then determining the constitutional question whether they are in conflict.

Constitutional Law -- Supremacy Clause -- Federal Pre-emption of State Law Regulating Prices of Home Heating Fuels

2. The provisions of the 1979 price gouging statute (General Business Law, § 396-r), which prohibit the sale of home heating fuel at an "unconscionably excessive price" during "periods of abnormal disruptions of the market", the Legislature having found that such an abnormal disruption existed for the 1979-1980 heating season, and which impose civil penalties for violations and provide for injunctive and other relief, establish de facto price controls upon home heating fuel and are thus invalid under the supremacy clause (US Const, art VI, § 2) since such State law is pre-empted by the Federal Emergency Petroleum Allocation Act of 1973 (US Code, tit 15, § 751 et seq., as amd) and its implementing directives and regulations which exempt home heating oil from price regulation, an area in which the Congress intended to occupy the entire field to the exclusion of the States; even if Congress [***3] did not completely occupy the field, section 396-r would still be violative of the supremacy clause since it is in direct conflict with the Federal law in that it stands as an obstacle to the accomplishment and execution of the full purpose and objectives of Congress and frustrates the full effectiveness of the Federal law, Congress having specifically found that free market forces will provide adequate or possibly greater protection for consumers and that deregulation of home heating fuel prices would not result in inequitable prices for any class of users; the Federal policy of achieving "equitable distribution" and "equitable prices" among "all regions and areas of the United States" may not be frustrated by a State's desire to protect a segment of its population and a State law cannot escape invalidation on pre-emption grounds because it is designed to promote a valid State interest.

Constitutional Law -- Statute Void for Vagueness -- Price Gouging on Sale of Home Heating Fuels

3. Provisions of section 396-r of the General Business Law which prohibit the sale of home heating fuel at an "unconscionably excessive price" during "periods of abnormal disruptions of the market",  [***4] although invalid under the supremacy clause (US Const, art VI, § 2) for being in conflict with a Federal law which exempts home heating oil from price regulation (Emergency Petroleum Allocation Act of 1973, US Code, tit 15, § 751 et seq., as amd), are not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad or violative of due process since the statute, a hybrid of civil and criminal remedies regulating commercial activity, intended to benefit the general public by permitting injunctive relief and restitution, and to punish the wrongdoer by the imposition of a fine, should be given an "equitable construction", as opposed to a strict construction in favor of the party against whom the penalty is sought to be imposed, and, under such liberal construction, the term "unconscionably excessive price" defined in the statute in terms of gross disparity between the price of goods or services and their value measured by prices at which they were available in the usual course of business prior to the disruption of the market or the difference between the price charged and the price at which the same goods or services were readily attainable by other consumers in the trade area provided the higher price [***5] is not attributable to higher cost, is sufficiently definite so as to inform one possessing "ordinary commercial knowledge" of what conduct is prohibited.

 

1979 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rochester Christian Church, Inc. v. New York Public Service Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Albany County


105 Misc. 2d 679; 432 N.Y.S.2d 800; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2708



October 21, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original action petitioner churches sought a judgment annulling and canceling an order from respondent State of New York Public Service Commission authorizing the assessment of a higher than domestic utility rate for services provided by respondent utility under N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 76. The churches sought a further judgment requiring the applicable domestic utility rate to be charged to churches operating adjunctive religious schools.


OVERVIEW: Each of the churches was duly organized and existing under state law and each conducted a school on church premises. The utility, which furnished gas and electric services, notified the churches that the operation of their schools was for other than religious purposes, because secular subjects were being taught as well as religious subjects. The churches appealed to the commission seeking a determination that the utility's practice was improper and not in accordance with § 76. At issue was whether the existence of a church-operated school, teaching secular and religious subjects, within the physical confines of the premises utilized as the church, was an operation so as to remove that church from the statutory mandate of § 76. The court granted the churches' petition on both accounts and held that: (1) because the interpretation of § 76 was one of pure statutory reading and analysis the court was not bound by the commission's interpretation; and (2) to apply the commission's interpretation would be to subvert the § 76 expressed public policy recognizing that the churches should have received the benefit of a lower gas and electric rate in order to foster their general well-being.


OUTCOME: The court granted the churches' petition for a judgment annulling the commission's order authorizing the assessment and charge of higher than domestic utility rates for services provided to the churches. The court also granted the churches' petitioner for a further judgment directing that domestic utility rates be charged to those churches operating religious schools as an adjunct to the operation of their churches.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Statutes -- Construction -- Administrative Agency

1. A court is not bound by the interpretation given a statute by an administrative agency when the interpretation did not require any special competence or expertise possessed by such agency.

Religious Corporations and Associations -- Utility Service at Domestic Rate

2. A church-operated school, teaching secular and religious subjects, within the physical confines of the premises utilized as a church is not an operation which will remove that church from the benefits conferred by section 76 of the Public Service Law, which requires religious organizations to be charged for gas and electric services at the same rate that domestic consumers within the same area are charged, since the purpose of the statute is to express a public policy that a house of worship should receive the benefit of a lower gas and electric rate in order to foster the general well-being of such a religious structure, and since a house of worship is more than a place to pray, it is a structure with a religious core out of which emanates multifaceted activities, all of which enhance its general religious goals; accordingly, the Public Service Commission's [***2] interpretation of the statute, which denied its benefits to such schools on the ground that the schools were conducted for other than religious purposes by the inclusion of secular subjects in the curriculum, unreasonably narrowed the scope of the statute to the extent that it would become obsolete.

 

1980 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Kilbourne v. State


Claim No. 63495


Court of Claims of New York


111 Misc. 2d 161; 443 N.Y.S.2d 538; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2976



October 20, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] In accordance with all of the foregoing, it is ordered, that the defendant's motion be in all respects granted and that the claim be and hereby is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant university filed a motion with the court (New York) to dismiss claimant student's amended claim on the ground that his causes of action based on defamation were barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: The university requested that the trial court dismiss the student's defamation actions on the ground that they were barred by the statute of limitations. The student's first cause of action arose on or about April 24, but he did not file his notice of intention until December 21. The court noted that a claim that arose out of a tortious act had to have been filed within 90 days of the act, unless notice of intention to file such claim was filed within that time period. The court dismissed the first cause of action because the student exceeded the 90-day period and the action could not be maintained. The court found that the student timely filed his second notice of intention. However, the school claimed that the student's action was not commenced within one year of the occurrence and was, therefore, time-barred. The court noted that N.Y. C.P.L.R. 215 required that libel and slander actions had to be commenced within one-year of the occurrence. The court dismissed the student's second cause of action because it was commenced beyond the one-year limitations period, and held that the student's notice of intention was not a claim because it failed to state a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the student's two defamation actions against the university.


HEADNOTES

State -- Claim against State -- Defamation Action

A defamation claim against the State filed in September, 1979 based upon allegedly defamatory statements made by members of the psychology department at a State university in September and December, 1977 concerning claimant's performance of psychological testings and experiments on school children as a graduate student is time barred since, although the notice of intention was timely filed, the action thereon was not commenced within the one-year Statute of Limitations applicable to defamation actions ( CPLR 215, subd 3) and no claim against the State may be allowed where such claim "would be barred by lapse of time" as between citizens of the State (NY Const, art III, § 19; Court of Claims Act, § 12, subd 2); the provision extending the time for filing a claim to two years after its accrual by the filing of a timely notice of intention (Court of Claims Act, § 10, subd 3) does not extend the time limitation beyond that specifically prescribed by law for the commencement [***2] of a particular type of action in view of the constitutional and statutory provisions prohibiting the award of a judgment against the State on a claim otherwise time barred; since the notice of intention did not set forth the precise statements alleged to be defamatory, it fails to state a cause of action ( CPLR 3016, subd [a]) and thus cannot be treated as the claim.

 

1981 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Obertance


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Bronx County


105 Misc. 2d 558; 432 N.Y.S.2d 475; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2547



October 17, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Both defendant's motions, are denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to dismiss the accusatory instrument pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L. 170.30 as defective, claiming that the statute he was arrested for violating, N.Y. Penal Law § 135.45, dealing with custodial interference, was unconstitutionally vague and indefinite because the term "protracted period" in the statute was not defined.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on a charge of custodial interference in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 135.45. Complainant, defendant's former wife, alleged that defendant took their two daughters from their legal custodian for a protracted period of time. Defendant moved to dismiss the accusatory instrument pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L. 170.30, claiming that the complaint was defective within the meaning of N.Y. C.P.L. 170.35, because the statute was unconstitutionally vague and indefinite since the term "protracted period" was not defined in the Penal Law and was capable of different meanings. The court found that a penal statute was not constitutionally defective if a word is not defined and that the everyday common sense meaning of the term was a lengthy or unusually long time. The court found that under the circumstances, defendant's taking his daughters for eight days without their custodial parent's consent was a protracted period and denied defendant's motion.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion, finding that the everyday common sense meaning of protracted period was a lengthy or unusually long time under the circumstances and that defendant's taking his daughters for eight days without the consent of their custodial parent while they were in school constituted a protracted period.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Custodial Interference -- "Protracted Period"

The unconstitutionality of a law must be demonstrated beyond a reasonable doubt and in order for a penal statute to be constitutional, it must be clear on its face, definite, explicit, objective and narrowly drawn and it must also give the general public an opportunity to know with reasonable certainty which activity is prohibited; accordingly, the custodial interference statute (Penal Law, § 135.45) which prohibits a relative from taking a child without the consent of the lawful guardian for a "protracted period" is not unconstitutionally vague and indefinite since a reasonable man would interpret the term "protracted period" to mean a lengthy or unusually long time under the circumstances and, therefore, defendant's unauthorized taking of his two daughters from their mother for a period of eight days constitutes a "protracted period" within the meaning of the statute.

 

1982 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Buffalo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Erie County


105 Misc. 2d 707; 432 N.Y.S.2d 982; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2570



October 14, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adult theater owner brought an action seeking an injunction and a judgment declaring that Buffalo, N.Y., Ordinance ch. 7, § 31 and Buffalo, N.Y., Ordinance ch. 70, § 16(17) were an unconstitutional infringement on his rights under U.S. Const. amend. I, V, and XIV. The theater owner claimed that his Fifth Amendment rights were violated by defendant city's requiring him to reveal information that might subject him to criminal prosecution.


OVERVIEW: During an investigation of the theater owner's operations, the theater owner was requested to complete a licensing form in order to stay in business. He partially completed the form and thereafter invoked his rights under the First, Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments with respect to other information requested on the form. The director of licenses rejected the form for failure to disclose the required information and the theater owner commenced an action for an injunction. The court granted the injunction and found that Buffalo, N.Y. Ordinance ch. 70, § 16(17)(e) was unconstitutional in that it required the theater owner to obtain an "adult" permit under his own name and to provide any information required by the director, in order to operate his movie theater. Because § 16(17)(e) subjected the exercise of the First Amendment freedom of speech to the prior restraint of a use permit without narrow, objective, and definite standards by which the director was to exercise his power, it was thus unconstitutional and was not a proper exercise of the police power. The other ordinance provisions were found to be legitimate enactments under the city's police power.


OUTCOME: The court granted the theater owner's request for an injunction.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Theatres and Shows -- Licenses -- Adult Movie Theatre -- Unconstitutional Disclosure of Owners' Names

An ordinance of the City of Buffalo, which requires a movie theatre to provide the name of the theatre's owner or principal stockholder and the names of all officers of the business operating the theatre on a registration form before being issued a license to operate, is unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff, an adult movie theatre showing sexually explicit films, since the registration information will be used to facilitate criminal prosecutions under the obscenity statutes (Penal Law, art 235) and compelling the disclosures contained within the registration form will confront those individuals with a substantial hazard of self incrimination in violation of the Fifth Amendment; in addition, the provision of the ordinance requiring an adult movie theatre to obtain an adult use permit after supplying "such other information as the director of licenses and permits shall require" is unconstitutional on its face and voids warranting the issuance of an injunction since an ordinance which subjects the exercise of First Amendment freedoms to the prior restraint of a use permit [***2] without narrow, objective and definite standards by which the licensing authority is to exercise its power is unconstitutional.

 

1983 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Female F. D.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Surrogate's Court of New York, Nassau County


105 Misc. 2d 866; 433 N.Y.S.2d 318; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2629



October 10, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner's teenager and child's father, initiated an action to set aside an adoption consent form signed by the teenager and dismiss an adoption proceeding.


OVERVIEW: While the teenager was in the hospital, she signed a consent to the adoption of the child. The teenager gave birth to the child. The child's father did not sign the consent form and was not identified on the child's birth certificate. The child was delivered to the adoptive parents. The teenager and the child's father were subsequently married and initiated an action to set aside the consent to adopt form and the adoption proceeding. The child's father contended that his consent to the adoption was required under N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 111. The court granted the petition to set aside the consent to adopt form, dismissed the adoption proceeding, and referred the matter to the family court. The court found that the child's father did not intend to abandon the child or to rid himself of parental obligations and parental rights. The court held that the child's father attempted to visit the child in the hospital, to be designated on the birth certificate, and to stop the adoption proceedings. The court found that the teenager's mother was primarily responsible for the adoption proceedings and rejected the attempts by the child's father to contact the teenager and the child.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition to set aside the adoption consent form, dismissed the adoption proceedings, and referred the matter to the family court for further proceedings.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Adoption -- Consent of Putative Father

The 1980 amendments to section 111 of the Domestic Relations Law which, as the result of the holding of the United States Supreme Court declaring that statute unconstitutional insofar as it permitted the adoption of an out-of-wedlock child on the consent of the natural mother but did not require a like consent from the putative father (see Caban v Mohammed, 441 U.S. 380), require the consent to an adoption from the father of an out-of-wedlock child under six months of age at the time of placement if the father has openly lived with the child or the child's mother for a continuous period of six months preceding placement, has openly held himself out to be the father during such period and has paid a fair and reasonable sum for expenses in connection with pregnancy or birth of the child, are too restrictive and unconstitutional as applied to petitioner putative father whose consent would not be required under the new statutory criteria even though he is a concerned, caring father entitled to the equal protection and due process rights granted him under the Caban case; the actions and conduct of the putative father in marrying the [***2] mother and desiring to keep the child negate any possible inference of an intent to abandon the child or to rid himself of parental obligations and parental rights; the consent of petitioner natural mother to the adoption, executed when she was 15 years old, is set aside because of the duress exercised upon her by her mother and, accordingly, the adoption proceeding instituted by respondents is dismissed.

 

1984 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Maksymenko


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Criminal Court of the City of New York, Queens County


105 Misc. 2d 368; 432 N.Y.S.2d 328; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2490



September 30, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was charged with misdemeanor offenses of harassment and resisting arrest, filed a motion to dismiss the complaint in the Criminal Court of the City of New York, Queens County (New York), based upon an alleged violation of his statutory and constitutional rights committed by the police.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was charged with misdemeanor offenses of harassment and resisting arrest, filed a motion to suppress his arrest and a motion to dismiss the complaint on the grounds that there was no probable cause or articulable suspicion to stop, detain, or make inquiries of defendant in the first instance, thus contending that any subsequent actions by police were in violation of his statutory and constitutional rights. The court held that: (1) defendant was entitled to a pretrial review of his claim that he was arrested without probable cause; (2) the arresting officer had no articulable basis to request that defendant identify himself, and there was no showing of a crime or other violation of law to establish the officer's right to detain defendant for purposes of the inquiry, and thus the arrests were unlawful; and (3) the so-called pushing of the officer by defendant in trying to regain entry to his vehicle was lawful conduct.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's motion to suppress the arrest as unlawful, and dismissed the complaint.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Crimes -- Arrest -- Pretrial Hearing on Issue of Reasonable Cause

A defendant arrested for the nonfelony offenses of harassment (Penal Law, § 240.25) and resisting arrest (Penal Law, § 205.30) based upon his refusal to produce identification to two police officers after he got out of his car to argue with the officers, both in plain clothes, whose unmarked car was blocking the road, is entitled to a pretrial hearing on the issue of reasonable cause for the arrest as part of a motion to suppress the arrest since such Fourth Amendment issue must be dealt with pretrial as a matter of law; defendant may move to dismiss a misdemeanor complaint where there exists some "legal impediment to conviction" ( CPL 170.30, subd 1, par [f]) and the court on such a motion may conduct a hearing and make findings of fact essential to a determination of the motion and the defendant has the burden of proving by a preponderance of the evidence every fact essential to support the motion ( CPL 210.45, subds 6, 7); accordingly, since the arresting officer has no articulable basis to request the defendant to identify himself and a citizen has no duty to respond to an officer's inquiry in the absence [***2] of articulable reasonable suspicion that unlawful activity is afoot, defendant's detention was unlawful and his ensuing conduct in "pushing" the arresting officer in trying to re-enter his car in order to extricate himself from a potentially combative situation was justified and lawful (cf. Penal Law, § 35.27) thus warranting suppression of the arrest for harassment and dismissal of the charge of resisting arrest.

 

1985 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Gardiner v. Stanley Orchards, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Ulster County


105 Misc. 2d 460; 432 N.Y.S.2d 335; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2527



September 30, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] All requests for any other relief by either party are denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town sought a preliminary injunction under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 6301 to restrain defendants, a corporation and an individual, from further preparation of a site located on their real estate in the town for construction of a mobile home and the placing of a mobile home on this site. Defendants filed a cross-motion for an order dismissing the town's complaint.


OVERVIEW: Defendants owned property in the town and filed an application for a building permit to place a mobile home on a parcel of land they owned, which was not part of a mobile home park or a mobile home subdivision. However, defendants never filed with the town clerk, or any other official of the town, permission in writing from all land owners within 500 feet of the boundaries of the property on which a mobile home was to be placed, which was required under the provisions of Town of Gardiner, N.Y., Local Law § 20, No. 3 (1972). Defendants contended that the local law was unconstitutional. Upon appeal, the court agreed and held that defendants sustained their burden of demonstrating that Town of Gardiner, N.Y., Local Law § 20, No. 3 (1972), was an unconstitutional consent requirement. The court converted the action into one for a declaratory judgment and held that the local law which defendants violated was void and not enforceable. Defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint was granted, and the town's motion for a preliminary injunction was denied, and the temporary restraining order was dissolved.


OUTCOME: The court found for defendants and converted the action into one for a declaratory judgment, holding that the local law which defendants violated was void and not enforceable as an unconstitutional consent requirement. The court granted defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint. The court also denied the town's motion for a preliminary injunction and dissolved the temporary restraining order.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Zoning -- Improper Mandatory Consent Requirement

Defendants' failure to exhaust their administrative remedies in making no effort to apply to respondent town board for a waiver from the requirements of a local law that they obtain the written permission of all landowners within 500 feet of the boundaries of their property before placing a mobile home on the property does not bar defendants from attacking the constitutionality of the local law on its face; accordingly, defendants have sustained their heavy burden of demonstrating the unconstitutionality of the local law since the mandatory unanimous consent requirement for the installation of a single mobile home, a use that is not a "nuisance" per se or "offensive", is an improper delegation of governmental zoning authority to private landowners without adequate standards to insure that the neighboring property owners will not act in an arbitrary or discriminatory manner and the fact that the local law vests the town board with discretion to waive the consent requirement does not remove the constitutional infirmity which makes the consent [***2] requirement and the local law void on its face.

 

1986 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re A.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Family Court of New York, New York County


105 Misc. 2d 254; 432 N.Y.S.2d 137; 1980 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2561



September 24, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother moved to indefinitely adjourn a child abuse proceeding on the ground that her constitutional privilege against self-incrimination would be violated if the child abuse trial were held before the termination of a criminal case against her concerning the same underlying acts.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner social services filed a child abuse petition against respondent mother alleging that her son was in danger of serious physical injury by her in that she caused the death of his younger brother.
